Saturday, 2:11 p.m. - Sealed Deckbuilding Exercise - pt. 1
----------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*
Because watching 1,800 people opening booster packs was just too much for me to handle, I grabbed a few myself and ripped them apart. I thought, if I were playing today, what would I do with this pool? I built a little something with it, but since I'm much worse at **Magic** than many people here, I decided to talk to some pros and see if they would build it like I had.


Later on today I'll be posting what a some pros did with the pool. But before that, here's your chance to shine. What would you do with this pile of cards?


Do you like the double [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies), double Krenko's Command and the [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer)? What about the solid, if a bit unexciting black cards? Blue might not have enough to stand on its own, but with 3 [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds), are some cards worth a splash? This pool asks a lot of questions, and some of the answers seem fuzzy.


Post your builds and thoughts on the message boards, and later today you can see how closely your take aligns with some of the top Grand Prix competitors here.


And remember, just because you can splash doesn't mean you have to . . . but sometimes you have to. Right?


 [![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//magic/sealeddeckbuilder/assets/Frontloader-Preview.jpg)](http://www.wizards.com/magic/sealeddeckbuilder/index.html?draftid=grand_prix_boston2012)
[![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/activity/sealedDeckBuilderButton_Static.jpg)](http://www.wizards.com/magic/sealeddeckbuilder/index.html?draftid=grand_prix_boston2012)


---


Round 3 Feature Match - Shaheen Soorani vs. Joshua Martinez
-----------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
Typically at a Grand Prix, players with recognizable names don't start playing till Round 4, on account of the byes piling up next to their names. With a field this large, though, that simply wasn't the case this weekend, as recognizable players like David Caplan, Gerard Fabiano, Richard Hoaen, Ben Lundquist, Max Tietze and Shaheen Soorani were each lined up to play in the third round.


From that stacked lineup Shaheen Soorani was plucked to face Joshua Martinez under the bright lights of the feature match area. Both players were grinders on the StarCity Games tournament circuit but had elected to try and wind their way through more than 1,800 players here this weekend.


To do so, Soorani had put together a White-Green deck full of large, bomby creatures like [Serra Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serra+Angel) and [Primordial Hydra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primordial+Hydra), while Martinez had matched utility creatures like [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero) and [Xathrid Gorgon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Xathrid+Gorgon) with a Red splash for Chandra the Firebrand and [Flames of the Firebrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flames+of+the+Firebrand). The power was certainly there on both sides of the table, and a strong draw from either player could tie their opponent up in knots quickly.


### Game 1


Martinez's [Aven Squire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Squire) drew first blood in the matchup of white-based decks, though Soorani hit harder with an [Attended Knight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Attended+Knight) followed by a [Prized Elephant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prized+Elephant).


"My favorite elephant," Soorani made sure we knew.


Meanwhile, Martinez was struggling with lands, stuck on just two while Soorani was summoning [Spiked Baloth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spiked+Baloth). [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism) took care of the pachyderm, but [War Priest of Thune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=War+Priest+of+Thune) unlocked it and made things pretty bad for Martinez.


Down to just four life after a massive attack, even [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero) wasn't enough to save the day, and Soorani took the first game with ease.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Rd%203%20Soorani.JPG)

*Shaheen Soorani figured out one way to beat an [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero) – kill his opponent before it matters.* 
"If you had drawn that third land earlier, I'm just dead. I can't beat [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero). You hit that third land, you're off to the races," Soorani said, ticking off the few outs he had in his deck.


Soorani 1 – Martinez 0


### Game 2


Another game, another [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero)...only this one was on time.


"There it is," Soorani said, attacking with just an [Aven Squire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Squire), afraid to play any of his larger threats.


"We can just do this all game if you want," Martinez said. "Play your elephant."


Instead, Soorani had a [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser), finding at least one creature he could play. It looked fine until Martinez dropped another bomb: [Xathrid Gorgon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Xathrid+Gorgon).


"Oh boy," Soorani said, exhaling as he put [Kitesail](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitesail) on his [Aven Squire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Squire) to take Martinez to 11.


Not that it much mattered. Martinez cast a [Healer of the Pride](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Healer+of+the+Pride) and froze the [Aven Squire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Squire), effectively shutting down Soorani's offense completely, even as he played [Silvercoat Lion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvercoat+Lion), [War Priest of Thune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=War+Priest+of+Thune) and [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) in succession. If he couldn't beat an [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero), tackling the Gorgon seemed pretty much impossible.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Rd%203%20wall%20of%20creatures.JPG)

*Good luck getting through that.* 
Not that Martinez had any offense of his own to speak of. His trio of [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero), [Healer of the Pride](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Healer+of+the+Pride) and [Xathrid Gorgon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Xathrid+Gorgon) were effective at keeping him alive, but didn't do much to put a dent in Soorani's life total.


Soorani did manage to resolve a [Primordial Hydra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primordial+Hydra) – for one counter – but it was a ticking time bomb that would soon throw itself under the [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero)'s power.




![Primordial Hydra++Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Primordial%20Hydra&options=)

![Primordial Hydra++Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Intrepid%20Hero&options=)
"I could just concede I guess, but I kind of want to see how you're going to kill me," Soorani thought out loud before playing [Predatory Rampage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Predatory+Rampage).


After the dust settled, only the [Silvercoat Lion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvercoat+Lion) was able to attack as a 6/6, but [Show of Valor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+of+Valor) kept Martinez' team from taking any casualties.


That was when Soorani started counting libraries to figure out if he should concede and Martinez flashed him the Chandra the Firebrand in his hand.


"Can you beat Chandra?" Martinez asked, even though he had no [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain)s in play.


"I'll concede to that," Soorani said, now fully aware of how Martinez could kill him.


Soorani 1 – Martinez 1


Game 3


Martinez had the first mulligan of the match, but he didn't seem too upset about it.


"I would mull to three if it was two lands [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero)," Martinez said.


"And I would lose that game," Soorani offered, clearly hoping to dodge the rare 1/1.



![Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Knight+of+Infamy)

Martinez kept his six cards, despite having a hand full of black spells and only [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) for mana. He quickly drew a [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp) and played [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) to race Soorani's [Aven Squire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Squire).


"If you don't do anything else for the rest of the game, I won't either," Martinez said. Soorani clearly wasn't going to take that bait and followed up with an [Attended Knight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Attended+Knight).


Martinez boosted his exalted forces with a [Duty-Bound Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duty-Bound+Dead) and a [War Priest of Thune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=War+Priest+of+Thune) – killing nothing – but Soorani had an on-curve [Serra Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serra+Angel) to really turn up the clock. When Yeva Forcemage pumped [Aven Squire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Squire) the following turn, Martinez fell to just six life and was in tons of trouble.


But a land off the top let him use [Essence Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Essence+Drain) to off Soorani's only nonwhite blocker allowing the [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) to continue its march to 20 damage. After four turns worth of [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) attacks, Soorani was at just four life, so one more unattended swing would seal the match for Martinez.


[Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser) gave Soorani the blocker he needed, but a [Mark of the Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mark+of+the+Vampire) on his [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) bumped Martinez to 10 life and turned the race completely on its hed. He fell to three on the attack, but Soorani found another green blocker to take the heat off for yet another turn.


"Come on [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk)," Soorani said has Martinez jumped to nine life on his next attack before playing [Battleflight Eagle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Battleflight+Eagle).


Instead it was [Garruk's Packleader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk%27s+Packleader) who jumped in front of the [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) as a third chump blocking Green creature fell by the wayside. Martinez cast a risky [Sign in Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sign+in+Blood), falling to seven, but he still had enough blockers to survive the swing back.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Rd%203%20Martinez.JPG)

*[Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy) gave Martinez a lot to smile about in Game 3.* 
[Plummet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plummet) removed [Battleflight Eagle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Battleflight+Eagle) from the equation, but Soorani could only squeeze through six power. With no other Green blocker forthcoming and no way to stop the rampaging [Knight of Infamy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Infamy), Soorani met an infamous end.


Soorani 1 – Martinez 2




---


Saturday, 3:51 p.m. - The Return of William "Huey" Jensen
---------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
One vote. One single vote from a selection committee member and the 2012 Hall of Fame Class would have been plus one William "Huey" Jensen. That's it. Just one vote.


It was the slimmest of margins, but it was enough to shine a spotlight on the old-school pro who was once one of the most feared players on the planet, and one of only a handful of players ever to defeat Kai Budde in the Top 8 of a Pro Tour.


But Jensen hasn't been heard from much since 2004, a fact that might have cost him some votes from players and selection committee members who simply never played against "Huey" in his heyday.


If this weekend goes well, though, they may just get their chance.


Jensen is making a quiet return to the game after almost a seven year hiatus from competitive **Magic** here at Grand Prix Boston.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/William%20Jensen%20027.JPG)

*William "Huey" Jensen is back on the scene at Grand Prix Boston more than eight years after his last Grand Prix Top 8.* 
"It's been a long time," Jensen said, unable to recall the last Grand Prix he even played in.


Part of the reason for his return is simple kismet – he has family in the area and happened to have some vacation time – but another part is his recent near miss into the Hall.


"In a sense, I guess so. You really reminisce and think of a lot of memories and people," said the player once known as "Huey" by his friends and fellow players. "It's good to see people, and I do miss being able to go to tournaments."


Back when Jensen could attend tournaments regularly, he was a force to be reckoned with. He racked up more than 200 lifetime pro points while winning two Grands Prix and a Pro Tour. He also Top 8ed another six Grands Prix and three other Pro Tours.


Jensen's current inability to go to tournaments has more to do with his location than his love of the game. He has lived on the small island of Curacao for the past several years with a contingent of some of the game's best players, such as Ben Rubin, Matt Linde, Eugene Harvey, Jelger Wiegersma, and others.


"It's very competitive," Jensen said of the Curacao crew's kitchen table drafts with a group that collectively has more Pro Tour Top 8s than most kitchen table games can ever dream of. "It gets the fire and the competitive juices flowing."


Jensen said if he were elected into the Hall of Fame, he would find a way to exercise that competitive fire every year with at least two Pro Tours and even a third if his schedule allowed. And, for his part, Jensen thinks he has a solid shot to make it in after falling just short.


"I think have I have a good chance next year, thanks in no part to this tournament," he said, ruing his weak pool and 0-2 start.


Jensen said he hopes to keep playing more over the next year, most likely at Grand Prix London in February where he says work will likely take him near enough to the Grand Prix to make it possible.


"I expected to do better than 0-2," Jensen said. "I don't think I'm going to win the tournament, but I think I still have the capability."




---


Round 4 Feature Match - Xavier Biron vs. Tzu Ching Kuo
------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*
Tzu Ching Kuo is one of the biggest names to come out of last week's World **Magic** Cup. Knocking out twelve wins in a row, Kuo helped lead his Chinese Taipei national team to a great win to clinch the coveted first World **Magic** Cup.


Xavier Biron is a strong Canadian **Magic**ian. Las month, he took down a Montreal PTQ with a solid Blue-Green Infect build. Though Mono-Green is the standard nowadays, Biron used [Blighted Agent](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blighted+Agent) and [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) he was allowed thanks to some [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)s, earning him a spot at the next Pro Tour.


The two players rolled, shuffled and drew for the first game.


### Game 1


Kuo led, but it was Biron who cast the first stone. A [War Priest of Thune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=War+Priest+of+Thune) off a [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp) and [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) got in there for two. This attack, combined with Kuo's second-turn [Sign in Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sign+in+Blood) gave the Canadian an early lead. [Crusader of Odric](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crusader+of+Odric) joined the Priest and after a pre-combat [Captain's Call](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain%27s+Call) on turn four, turning the Crusader into a 5/5, Kuo was quickly down to 9. And he was yet to cast a creature.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/D1R4%20Biron.JPG)

*Game 1 goes quickly to Xavier Biron* 
Kuo found his fourth land and tapped out for a [Shimian Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shimian+Specter) to block, but Biron flashed the [Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder) sitting in his hand before he untapped. At the first opportunity, Biron murdered the Specter and swung again, this time with the help of the 1/1 Soldiers. That was a whopping ten damage. Just like that, we were ready for the second game. A fifth-turn kill in Sealed is not a common occurrence, but with a little land stumbles and a little murdering, it can happen.


Xavier Biron 1 – 0 Tzu Ching Kuo


### Game 2


Kuo's first-turn [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) revealed this hand from Biron: [Dark Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Favor), [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds)[Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero), [Captain's Call](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain%27s+Call), [Bloodthrone Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodthrone+Vampire), [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp), [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains). The Taiwanese took the wannabe [Spectral Procession](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spectral+Procession) and followed with a 3/2 [Crimson Muckwader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crimson+Muckwader), then a [Reckless Brute](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reckless+Brute). The 1/1 Vampire came out from Biron and traded with the Brute. The Canadian was down to 14 when he begun to stabilize. Kuo had not added any friends for Muckwader and Biron had an [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero) and [Shimian Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shimian+Specter).


After some thought, Kuo attacked in for three and used a [Volcanic Geyser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Geyser) to kill the [Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intrepid+Hero), unsettling Biron's stabilization process. Biron went to 11 and then 8 the following turn. Though far behind (it was 8-20 with Kuo leading), Biron had cleared his opponent's hand with [Shimian Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shimian+Specter) and played a [Dark Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Favor) on Ajani's Sunstriker to get back into the game. The cat-and-ghost attack made the totals 11-12 for Biron. After that turn, the cat stayed indoors because Kuo's [Hellion Crucible](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellion+Crucible) had the right amount of counters to make it dangerous to venture out on the ground. But the Specter still plinked Kuo down to 9, while ensuring Kuo was playing off the top of his library. Biron added extra insurance with a [Captain's Call](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain%27s+Call) before passing the turn back.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/D1R4%20Kuo.JPG)

*World **Magic** Cup Team Champion Tzu Ching Kuo can't find a way to deal with his opponents flyers.* 
Kuo made his 4/4 Hellion at the end of his opponent's turn and cast [Liliana's Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana%27s+Shade). But still without flyers, Kuo couldn't keep anything in his hand. Anything he kept would end up removed from the game. He dug for an answer with [Sign in Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sign+in+Blood), but still came up short. He sighed a bit as he passed the turn back. He knew this might be his last turn.


Biron untapped, confidently slammed a second [Dark Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Favor) on his Specter and sent in a big ol' alpha strike. Kuo only needed to glance at all the sideways creatures before he was ready to call it quits.


Xavier Biron 2 – 0 Tzu Ching Kuo


Advancing to 4-0, the Canadian Xavier Biron had taken a decisive win off the big up-and-comer and World **Magic** Cup Team Champion, Tzu Ching Kuo.




---


Round 5 Feature Match - Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa vs. Craig Krempels
-------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
"Long time," Craig Krempels said, greeting All-World All-Star Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa at the start of Round 5. Surely an understated welcome when facing off against a Hall of Famer still in his prime.


But at 4-0 with solid decks at their fingers, it's not like either player was hurting for confidence in their ability to win.


Krempels had a fast, beefy Red-Green deck highlighted by [Yeva, Nature's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yeva%2C+Nature%27s+Herald). He could hit fast and he could hit hard, but he lacked anything truly bomby.


Damo da Rosa, on the other hand, had all of the bombs in a White-Black deck that was somewhat reminiscent of the deck that he fell short with at Grand Prix Sao Paolo. Practicing the weekend before the Players Championship, the Brazilian was certainly hoping for a better result in Boston.


### Game 1


With a lightning quick pace from both players, the board was quickly cluttered with creatures, especially for Damo da Rosa, who curved [Aven Squire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Squire) into [Attended Knight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Attended+Knight) into [Bloodhunter Bat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodhunter+Bat) into [Shimian Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shimian+Specter), while Krempels started with only a [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser).


In fact, Krempels start was so stunted that, even with an overwhelming board presence early on and Krempels' lone creature tapped from attacking, the Brazilian was weary when making his next attacks. Still, he saw no combat tricks after attacking with just his fliers and hit Krempels to 10.


However, Krempels did have a trick of a sorts at the end of turn that made Damo da Rosa's non-attack with his ground creatures look positively sage-like, as [Yeva, Nature's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yeva%2C+Nature%27s+Herald) jumped on to the battlefield to shove seven power worth of attackers in Damo da Rosa's face. [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser) traded with the [Attended Knight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Attended+Knight) and its squire before Krempels cast [Furnace Whelp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Furnace+Whelp).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Round%205%20PVDDR.JPG)

*Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa had a lot to ponder over against Craig Krempels in Round 5.* 
But Damo da Rosa was firing on all cylinders, hitting [Captain of the Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain+of+the+Watch) right on time. [Furnace Whelp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Furnace+Whelp) traded with the [Shimian Specter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shimian+Specter), but Krempels otherwise dropped to just six life. When Damo da Rosa declined to block Yeva on the next attack, it set up a lethal swing for the Hall of Famer.


Damo da Rosa 1 – Krempels 0


### Game 2


After being run over by a curve of hard hitting beats, Krempels opted to play with a sigh. His Green and Red deck was built for speed, but had stumbled in the early turns in Game 1.


And speed it did, as [Arbor Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arbor+Elf) enabled a [Rummaging Goblin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rummaging+Goblin) in short order, but he had no follow up.


Instead, it was Damo da Rosa who took control once again, trading his [War Falcon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=War+Falcon) with the [Arbor Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arbor+Elf) and casting a very dangerous [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk).


With a "hee-ya," Krempels cast and attacked with [Flinthoof Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flinthoof+Boar). Attempting to race [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) was usually a losing proposition, but it was all Krempels had for now.


Then Damo da Rosa played possibly the sickest [Sign in Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sign+in+Blood) I've ever seen, drawing both [Captain of the Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain+of+the+Watch) and [Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sublime+Archangel). When he also had [Cathedral of War](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cathedral+of+War) on his next turn, the [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) was suddenly hitting for five.


Yup, five.




![Primordial Hydra++Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Primordial%20Hydra&options=)

![Primordial Hydra++Intrepid Hero](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Intrepid%20Hero&options=)
Forced into action, Krempels used [Titanic Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Titanic+Growth) and [Prey Upon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prey+Upon) to kill the [Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sublime+Archangel) ... just in time for Damo Da Rosa to play what would have surely been a backbreaking [Captain of the Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain+of+the+Watch). If the [Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sublime+Archangel) were still around, the [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) could have attacked as a 9/10.


"Yeah, why wouldn't it be that," Krempels said, sighing at his board of [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser), [Flinthoof Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flinthoof+Boar), [Rummaging Goblin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rummaging+Goblin) and newly cast [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer).


Wary of the death-dealing Goblin, Damo da Rosa attacked with just a single Soldier token after casting [Angelic Benediction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Benediction). Krempels fell to six life before using [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer) to kill [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) (sacrificing the [Rummaging Goblin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rummaging+Goblin)).


A second activation of the [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer) removed the [Captain of the Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain+of+the+Watch) while another [Flinthoof Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flinthoof+Boar) suddenly put Damo da Rosa and his bevy of bombs on the back foot.


Now with just two Soldier tokens on the table, Damo da Rosa shifted to chump blocking mode with a hand was just five lands.


To recap, Damo da Rosa cast [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk), [Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sublime+Archangel) and [Captain of the Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain+of+the+Watch) ... and was now losing, thanks in small part to some pretty severe flooding and in large part to Krempels relentlessly tearing through his team.


When another land was all that greeted him on top of his deck, Damo da Rosa had somehow lost a game where he cast a multitude of the format's best cards over a series of several turns.


"I guess you got an above-average pool," Krempels said.


"It's pretty good," Damo da Rosa offered back.


Damo da Rosa 1 – Krempels 1


### Game 3


[Slumbering Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slumbering+Dragon) stared things off for Krempels, though it wouldn't be involved in the action for some time. Or, actually, at all (foreshadowing!).


Meanwhile [Crippling Blight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crippling+Blight), well, crippled a [Deadly Recluse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadly+Recluse) and [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear) killed a [Duskmantle Prowler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskmantle+Prowler).


Then Krempels cast his bomb, flashing in a [Yeva, Nature's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yeva%2C+Nature%27s+Herald). Damo da Rosa attempted to kill the Green legend with [War Falcon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=War+Falcon) plus [Show of Valor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+of+Valor), but [Chandra's Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chandra%27s+Fury) killed it before the trick resolved.


Krempels then added a [Canyon Minotaur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Canyon+Minotaur) to the battlefield, further squeezing Damo da Rosa's already taxed board.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Round%205%20Krempels.JPG)

*Craig Krempels was clearly unfazed sitting across from a Hall of Famer and Players Championship competitor.* 
[Captain of the Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain+of+the+Watch) was certainly an answer, but Krempels had already shown that his deck was full of tricks ... including the [Titanic Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Titanic+Growth) he used to save Yeva from the blocks of two Soldier tokens. Once again, Damo da Rosa was in a hole.


[Battleflight Eagle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Battleflight+Eagle) let Damo da Rosa get in his first attack of the game – ticking up the [Slumbering Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slumbering+Dragon) by one – but he was still pretty far behind. [Bladetusk Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bladetusk+Boar) only served to deepen the Hall of Famer's hole.


He attempted to fight back with a [Bloodhunter Bat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodhunter+Bat), but a hand full of lands made that difficult, especially as Krempels continued to use [Rummaging Goblin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rummaging+Goblin) to tear through his deck.


[Flinthoof Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flinthoof+Boar) upped the pressure even more, forcing Damo da Rosa to reluctantly start blocking with his [Captain of the Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain+of+the+Watch). After the attack, Damo da Rosa's board was clear while Krempels still had his [Bladetusk Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bladetusk+Boar). Damo da Rosa tried a desperation [Sign in Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sign+in+Blood), but finding no removal for the intimidating Boar, he was out of options...and out of life


Damo da Rosa 1 – Krempels 2




---


Saturday, 6:10 p.m. - Sealed Deck Exercise - pt. 2
--------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*
If you hadn't yet seen the Sealed Pool from earlier, scroll up, or click [here](#1) if you're lazy. I gave this list to a couple Pros to see what they would do with it. First up was Sam Black.


Immediately Black threw out the blue, saying, "the good cards are doubles and there's not enough of the rest." Even though the white pile gave him pause, his first build after perusing everything was full of red and black. He liked the aggressive look of it, but when I asked was what missing, as he piled the cards back together, he muttered, "Cards." There were about nineteen playables, and a splash wasn't going to make up for the deck's deficiencies. Red was aggressive but lacked removal and enough speed to not worry about such removal-lacking.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Sealed%20Ex%202%20Black%2C%20Martell%2C%20Vidugiris.JPG)

*Tom Martell, Sam Black, and Gaudenis Vidugiris* 
Black then vacillated among three colors: red, white and green. He did every iteration – White-Red, White-Green, Red-Green – before he stared at the three [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds) and put all ingredients into the pot. Black seemed the most excited about this build. "You've got the synergy of the [Healer of the Pride](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Healer+of+the+Pride), [Krenko's Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krenko%27s+Command) and [Predatory Rampage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Predatory+Rampage)." It was about this time that everyone else at the table started turning towards Black looking at what he had constructed. Tom Martell, Gaudenis Vidugiris, and Brian Kibler all cocked their heads at the extremely greedy brew Black had put together. Kibler took one look and said "Are you trolling the world with that?"


Martell's eyes widened seeing the aggressive red and white and tried to make a Red-White deck work shoving the green to one side. Cards that Black had previously cut were thrown back into the mix. [Silvercoat Lion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvercoat+Lion)s, [Warclamp Mastiff](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warclamp+Mastiff) and [Kindled Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kindled+Fury) were all being considered. "Whenever I see a [Trumpet Blast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trumpet+Blast), I'm all in." Martell continued, "And the [Warclamp Mastiff](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warclamp+Mastiff) goes well with the [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies). There's a good tokens deck here." Kibler remained unconvinced.


"Tokens?! You've got two [Krenko's Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krenko%27s+Command). That's it. And are you really playing [Ajani's Sunstriker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ajani%27s+Sunstriker), [Krenko's Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krenko%27s+Command) and [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary)?" Black was quick to point out all of the cards that went well with those Commands. [Healer of the Pride](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Healer+of+the+Pride), [Crusader of Odric](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crusader+of+Odric), [Griffin Protector](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griffin+Protector) all worked well, and this was the same rationale that was later used to keep in [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary).


Black went back and forth between two colors and three. But finally, after realizing that a splash of blue wasn't worth the shaky mana because all the cards he wanted were five-drops, he seemed content with his three-color build. He wasn't too happy to be relying so much on the two [Healer of the Pride](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Healer+of+the+Pride), but as long as they didn't immediately die to a [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear), the life-gain would give him the time he needed to set up for a perfect [Predatory Rampage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Predatory+Rampage).


The deck Black settled on looked like this:

[Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BSublime%5D+%5BArchangel%5D)


40 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Evolving+Wilds)


















The last card was still being shuffled around, but Black liked it the best out of his other iterations. However, he wouldn't have swapped this pool for the one he's currently using. Martell on the other hand, said he'd definitely trade this pool for his own and was ready to force the red and white and drop the Spiders, Wurm, Rampage, [Rancor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rancor), [Farseek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Farseek), Courser and the Elf. Though he didn't make an exact build, it's safe to say it would've contained the [Silvercoat Lion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Silvercoat+Lion)s, [Kindled Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kindled+Fury), [Hellion Crucible](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellion+Crucible), [Volcanic Strength](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Strength) (Oh, I love [Volcanic Strength](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Strength)") and nary a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) in sight.


If Black's deck is a little greedy for you, or Martell's ideas too aggressive for your Sealed tastes, perhaps Jon Finkel's build is good for what ails you. Finkel was markedly more decisive, and never really strayed from his first impressions. He quickly laid out the colors, tossing aside any cards he didn't want to play.


"I can't imagine not playing White here. The blue is fine. The red has good beatdown, but isn't deep. The green just isn't enough."



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Sealed%20Ex%202%20Black%2C%20Martell.JPG)

*Sam Black and Tom Martell* 
After making no real remarks about black, he laid the color back out, ordering by mana cost, then put his hand to his chin. He matched those cards with the white ones and then the Hall of Famer started counting cards. He only had to cut a few to get the deck to fighting weight. Out came the [Glorious Charge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glorious+Charge); out came the [Ring of Xathrid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ring+of+Xathrid); out came the [Rise from the Grave](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rise+from+the+Grave).


"I'm not real happy to be playing the Lions, but they are necessary." I asked him if he had trouble with the large amount of four drops represented on the table, as there were two [Healer of the Pride](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Healer+of+the+Pride), [Griffin Protector](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griffin+Protector), [Bloodhunter Bat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodhunter+Bat), [Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sublime+Archangel), [Divine Verdict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divine+Verdict), Liliana's Shade, [Duskmantle Prowler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskmantle+Prowler) and [Mark of the Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mark+of+the+Vampire) all crowding the slot. He started to move the double-colored spells into the five-drop slot took a random half of the pile and moved it into the empty five-drop slot. "If the curve looked like this, people would still be happy to play this deck."



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Sealed%20Ex%202%20Finkel.JPG)

*Finkel creating his sample deck from the Sealed Deckbuilder Pool* 
It looked as if Finkel grabbed the two deepest colors, saw they didn't look awful next to each other and just went to town. On the three [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds), Finkel said the only card he would be excited to splash at all was [Switcheroo](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Switcheroo) and that it wasn't worth it for him. "It's good, but it's not that good. And I don't need it." He finished with, "Just because you can splash doesn't mean you should." Words I've never lived by, but probably should. The final deck from Jon Finkel looked like this:







#### Jon Finkel


#####

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Plains)


















The land count and distribution is speculative as we didn't talk much about it. Finkel did say that he would likely play a couple of the Wilds, but probably not all of them as he didn't want to get too slowed down.


I did talk to one last person who never minds being slowed down by a couple extra colors, but that will wait until the last installment. If you are a budding Sealed deck-builder, you might not want to read it; it's not for the faint of heart. Because when you give Luis Scott-Vargas three [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds), you never know what'll happen.




---


Saturday, 6:29 p.m. - Grinding through Grinder Data
---------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
Grinders – the single-elimination, no-room-for-error tournaments that award three byes – are often a fun side event from a coverage perspective, a way to highlight some performances and show some neat decklists if the grinders happen to be from a constructed format.


But because of the massive size of Grand Prix Boston-Worcester, we've actually been able to mine quite a bit of data out of the 21 grinders that fired on Friday.


For example, of the winning decks, I can tell you that [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) and [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest)s were the most played cards, while [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)s and [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain)s lagged behind the rest.


I can tell you that [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism) was easily the most played card, with 16 copies spread out among 21 decks. I can also tell you not a single [Craterize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Craterize) made the cut, in case you were curious about [Demolish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Demolish)'s younger, far less talented cousin.


So for those stat-heads out there and people looking to get a let up in *M13* Limited, here's a fire hose of information about the decks that did the best when their backs were against the wall.




|  |
| --- |
| **Plains and Islands in decks** |
| * Decks with at least one [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) (out of 21 possible): 14
* Decks with at least one [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island): 5
 |
|  |

Blue was easily the least represented color, and also had the ignominy of being the only color that not a single player splashed in their winning deck list. Meanwhile, White was splashed everywhere, mostly for [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) and...




![Pacifism++Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Pacifism&options=)

![Pacifism++Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Centaur%20Courser&options=)


|  |
| --- |
| **Popular Cards** |
| * Most popular common card: [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism) (16 copies)
* Second most popular common card: [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser) (12) and [Timberpack Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timberpack+Wolf) (12)
 |
|  |

Right behind them were [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear) (11), [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) (10) and [Essence Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Essence+Drain) (10). No other card had double-digit copies in among the winning decklists.




|  |
| --- |
| **Number of lands played (lands per Deck):** |
| * 15: 1 deck
* 16: 3 decks
* 17: 16 decks
* 18: 1 deck
 |
|  |

The 15 land-deck was an aggressive Black-Red deck with three [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies) and only two cards that cost five mana. The 18 land deck, interestingly enough, also had two [Arbor Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arbor+Elf) and a [Farseek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Farseek), but also had two [Rummaging Goblin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rummaging+Goblin)s and was three colors.




|  |
| --- |
| **Most popular individual cards** |
| * Most popular uncommon: [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) (8 copies)
* Most popular rare: [Captain of the Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain+of+the+Watch) (4 copies)
* Most popular mythic rare: [Primordial Hydra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primordial+Hydra) (2 copies)
 |
|  |

There were more [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring)s in the 21 winning decklists than [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds) (7), [Spiked Baloth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spiked+Baloth)s (8), [Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder)s (6), [Prey Upon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prey+Upon) (6), [Primal Clay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primal+Clay) (6) and [Arbor Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arbor+Elf) (5), for example. There were more [Captain of the Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Captain+of+the+Watch) than [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist) (3), [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies) (3), [Scroll Thief](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scroll+Thief) (3) and [Divination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divination) (2).




![Captain of the Watch++Primordial Hydra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Captain%20of%20the%20Watch&options=)

![Captain of the Watch++Primordial Hydra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Primordial%20Hydra&options=)
*What do you call seeing these two cards in your sealed pool? A good start.*


|  |
| --- |
| **Most popular card by color** |
| * Most popular White card: [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism) (16)
* Most popular Green card: [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser) (12)
* Most popular Black card: [Essence Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Essence+Drain) (10)
* Most popular red card: [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear) (11)
* Most popular blue card: [Unsummon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unsummon) (6)
 |
|  |

Green had 11 cards that were as popular or more so than [Unsummon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unsummon) among the winning decklists.


Non-rare/mythic cards that had only one entry among the 21 winning decklists: [War Priest of Thune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=War+Priest+of+Thune), [War Falcon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=War+Falcon), [Vedalken Entrancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vedalken+Entrancer), [Trumpet Blast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trumpet+Blast), [Tormented Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormented+Soul), [Torch Fiend](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Torch+Fiend), [Switcheroo](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Switcheroo), [Safe Passage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Safe+Passage), [Rise from the Grave](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rise+from+the+Grave), [Ring of Xathrid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ring+of+Xathrid), [Ring of Evos Isle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ring+of+Evos+Isle), [Ring of Kalonia](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ring+of+Kalonia), [Plummet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plummet), [Pillarfield Ox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pillarfield+Ox), [Mindclaw Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mindclaw+Shaman), [Kraken Hatchling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kraken+Hatchling), [Knight of Glory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Glory), [Jayemdae Tome](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jayemdae+Tome), [Jace's Phantasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%27s+Phantasm), [Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit), [Glorious Charge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glorious+Charge), [Furnace Whelp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Furnace+Whelp), [Duskdale Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskdale+Wurm), [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress), [Bond Beetle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bond+Beetle), and [Augur of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Augur+of+Bolas).


There were a total of 26 non-rare/mythic cards that had just one copy in the winning decks.


Most copies of any one card in any single deck: 3 ([Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser), [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies), [Deadly Recluse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadly+Recluse), [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear), [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism), [Timberpack Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timberpack+Wolf))


Surprisingly, the three copies of [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies) in one deck were the only three copies to see play in any Grinder winning deck.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/mogg_flunkies.jpg)

*"So, uh, we attack, right guys?"* 
Want more? If you've gotten this far in the article, you probably do! If so, here's a chart of every card (besides basic lands) played by the Grinder winning decklists along with the number of copies of each one played, in order from most played to least. Enjoy!

Round 6 Feature Match - Pat Cox vs. David Shiels
------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*
Both Pat Cox and David Shiels have three Grand Prix Top 8s under their belts. Though the highest Cox has finished is 2nd at Grand Prix Austin, Shiels took down the entire Grand Prix Dallas-FortWorth. Both Texas GPs ... interesting.


### Game 1


Cox started off showing a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) and a [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp) but he stumbled after that. He had kept a hand with both [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) and [Elvish Archdruid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Archdruid), but not finding the third land spelled trouble (with a capital "T" and rhymes with "V" and that stands for [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk)). Shiels already showed a [Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit) and a Liliana's Shade by the time Cox found a land. But even that draw taunted Cox as it was an [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds) and didn't help him cast anything he needed to.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/GP%20Bos%20-%20D1R6%20Cox.jpg)

*David Cox* 
Cox searched out a [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp) rather than a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) because if any three-drop can get you back into a game, it's that crazy flying, lifelinking, deathtouching beatstick. But since his new draw had revealed another black three-drop, [Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder), Cox waited to kill the [Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit) on Shiels next attack. And that land had come just in time. After Shiels's attack step, Cox had dropped to 6.



![Talrand, Sky Summoner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Talrand%2C+Sky+Summoner)

The following turn Cox played the vampire and immediately used a [Prey Upon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prey+Upon) to kill the Shade (while gaining two life for his trouble, with "T"s rhyming with "P"s for [Prey Upon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prey+Upon), et al.). Shiels cast an [Essence Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Essence+Drain) on the [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) and the last two creatures on the board were two innocuously cast [Giant Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Scorpion)s for Shiels. They didn't seem like much when Shiels was busy making the life totals 6-23. But maybe the two 1/3s could be just enough to seal the deal for David Shiels.


Cox played an [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) and had a good-looking grip of [Essence Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Essence+Drain), [Liliana of the Dark Realms](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Dark+Realms) and a [Mark of the Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mark+of+the+Vampire), but Shiels made him discard everything but the Drain with a [Mind Rot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mind+Rot). The next turns were consumed with trades for one damage back and forth until it was 3-19 and David Shiels cast a [Talrand, Sky Summoner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Talrand%2C+Sky+Summoner). Cox laid an [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) and continued the one-damage trade-offs, 2-18.


With another draw step, Cox thought he might finally be out of the woods. He summoned an [Arbor Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arbor+Elf), then a [Phyrexian Hulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Hulk) the turn after. But when only the Hulk was left to block, Shiels used the final two cards in his hand – [Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder) and a [Duty-Bound Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duty-Bound+Dead). With Cox at two and with nothing to block but a murdered Hulk, this dribbling game came to a close when an exalted Scorpion scuttled over to give the final sting to Pat Cox.


David Shiels 1 – 0 Pat Cox


"That is definitely the most damage my [Giant Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Scorpion) will do all day." David Shiels smiled. The two shuffled up and played game number two.


### Game 2


Shiels cast the first spell of the game in a [Duty-Bound Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duty-Bound+Dead), but Cox immediately obsoleted it with a [Knight of Glory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Glory).


"Well that's lame." Shiels was exaggeratedly defeated.




![Duty-Bound Dead++Knight of Glory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Duty-Bound%20Dead&options=)

![Duty-Bound Dead++Knight of Glory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Knight%20of%20Glory&options=)
The Knight beat Shiels uncontested for a few turns to take him to 14. Shiels attacked into Cox's new 2/2 [Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit) with his 1/3 skeleton, a possible bluff, but Cox played it safe – assuming [Crippling Blight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crippling+Blight) – and took the damage.


[Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit) from Cox only had [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) and [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp)s to play with and was severely outmatched by Shiels's [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)-aided Bandit. But with the help of Cox's [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) it was the last Bandit standing. When Cox followed up with a [Ravenous Rats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ravenous+Rats) and Shiels pitched the Blight, Cox nodded and said, "I knew you had it."


Throughout this Game Two, just as they had both been drowning in mana last game, they were both dehydrated here. It was at least turn seven and both players had three lands to their names. The [Giant Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Scorpion) from Shiels should have brought the game to a standstill, but the [Knight of Glory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Glory) was causing Shiels fits. The two-drop dealt twelve damage by itself. However, the Scorpion was still useful with the help of exalted triggers, and kept Shiels afloat. When the [Bloodhunter Bat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodhunter+Bat) came down for the Grand Prix Dallas-FortWorth winner, it was all but even at 11-10 – barely in Cox's favor.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/GP%20Bos%20-%20D1R6%20Shiels.jpg)

*Shiels wins an important match over cox* 
Better news for Shiels came in the form of a [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton) next turn. After a little pumping it was able to finally kill the Knight. Cox was happy to trade, because at the rate the game was progressing giving the artifact +1/+1 each turn would make it very big, very quick.


Cox had on his board [Ravenous Rats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ravenous+Rats), [Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit), [Attended Knight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Attended+Knight) and a 1/1 Solider token on his team. They all stared down Shiels's [Bloodhunter Bat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodhunter+Bat), [Duty-Bound Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duty-Bound+Dead) and [Giant Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Scorpion). Cox went for the win with a [Mark of the Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mark+of+the+Vampire) on his Knight, but Shiels was holding the goods. He cast a [Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder) on the intended target and then coasted to victory on the wings of a 2/2 Bat and an [Essence Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Essence+Drain) to speed the process along.


David Shiels 2 – 0 Pat Cox


A humble [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton) was what turned a struggling Shiels into a happy Shiels. And though Pat Cox now drops to 4-2, David Shiels jumps up to 5-1.




---


Round 7 Feature Match - Stefan Ellsworth vs. Yuuya Watanabe
-----------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
"I want to be on camera!" Stefan Ellsworth, a Boston native said as soon as he sat down.


If he keeps winning, he might just get his wish. As one of the few remaining undefeated players, Ellsworth was just one match win away from locking up an invite back tomorrow, something he had never accomplished before.


But standing in his way was "the player who is about to destroy me," as Ellsworth eloquently guessed before Yuuya Watanabe even sat down. As one of the 16 players qualified for the 2012 Players Championship and the captain of the Japanese national team at the World **Magic** Cup, Watanabe was certainly one of the last players in the room anyone wants to face, especially since he had yet to drop a match today.


### Game 1


In what looked like a Green-Red deck splashing Black, Watanabe kept a fairly speculative hand, with no red mana and only an [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) as a castable card.


He was soundly punished when he missed his fourth land drop and immediately begin drawing five and seven drops...including the [Duskdale Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskdale+Wurm) he was forced to discard, slumping in his seat as [Knight of Glory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Glory) and [Wind Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wind+Drake) were beating down from across the table backed by [Guardians of Akrasa](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Guardians+of+Akrasa).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Round%207%20Watanabe.JPG)

*This is Yuuya Watanabe not casting spells. It looks kind of like Yuuya Watanabe casting spells, but with less to do and more cards in hand.* 
A [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) gave a sudden ray of hope, letting him cast [Firewing Phoenix](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Firewing+Phoenix) to stand in the way. But even that was short lived as [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) removed it from play.


Sighing as he drew yet another uncastable card, Watanabe was quietly scooped up his cards, pinned in by his mana.


Ellsworth 1 – Watanabe 0


### Game 2


Watanabe saw a very similar hand in the second game as he did the first, with a series of four and five drops plus two lands and an [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary). Never one to second-guess himself based on past actions, Watanabe kept it once again...


...and immediately started drawing cards he couldn't cast again, missing land number three while drawing another four drop and shaking his head again. He also used his [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds) to find a [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp) rather than the [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) that would have unlocked much of his hand.


Ellsworth, meanwhile cast a [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton) and [Ajani's Sunstriker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ajani%27s+Sunstriker), starting his attacks when the pair were both 2/2s. He even added a second Sunstriker to the board.



![Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Chronomaton)

That was when Watanabe finally found his fourth land and first [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain). [Bladetusk Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bladetusk+Boar), however, wasn't terribly impressive at this stage of the game, especially after it died to [Divine Verdict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divine+Verdict) on the next attack.


But a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) was just what the doctor ordered. Land number five and [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) number two enabled [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime), which not only killed [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton), but gave a pretty fantastic blocker. For a moment it looked like he might be able to turn the match around.


Yet Ellsworth wasn't out of his own tricks. [Clone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Clone) copied [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) and destroyed Watanabe's lone [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain), stranding a group of red cards in the Japanese player's hand. When Watanabe found [Essence Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Essence+Drain), Ellsworth had the [Negate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Negate) to keep his [Clone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Clone) chugging along.


A few turns of three-point exalted attacks from the [Clone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Clone), and Ellsworth had qualified for his first Grand Prix Day Two, doing it while stepping over one of the best players in the universe, nonetheless.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Round%207%20Ellsworth.JPG)

*Stefan Ellsworth not only is making his first Day 2 at a Grand Prix, but he's doing it in style, going 7-0 and defeating one of the best players on the planet.* 
"I don't know what to say. Holy crap," Ellsworth said, beaming from ear to ear. "[Sorry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sorry) about that. Good luck."


Ellsworth wouldn't need any luck of his own to move on. At 7-0, he was riding high at the top of the tournament.


Ellsworth 2 – Watanabe 0




---


Saturday, 8:02 p.m. - Quick Hits: What card has been your MVP so far today?
---------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Quick%20Questions%20MVP%20Estratti.JPG)*Samuel Estrati - "[Primordial Hydra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primordial+Hydra)"* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Quick%20Questions%20MVP%20Black.JPG)*Sam Black – "[Krenko, Mob Boss](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krenko%2C+Mob+Boss) (he really wanted to say [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton)"* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Quick%20Questions%20MVP%20Lee.JPG)*Jackie Lee - "[Roaring Primadox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Roaring+Primadox)"* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Quick%20Questions%20MVP%20Duke.JPG)*Reid Duke – "[Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder)"*
