---


Round 8 Feature Match - Ben Murray vs. Samuele Estratti
-------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*
You know, it wasn't long ago that I was rooting for a relatively unknown Italian player named Samuele Estratti as he battled uphill at Pro Tour Austin with his All-In Red deck in 2009. Adorned with a red scarf, Estratti almost made it to the Top 8, but for a few draft missteps.


Nowadays, if you don't know Mr. Estratti, it's because you've have your head too close to a [Glacial Chasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glacial+Chasm), if you catch my drift. He won Pro Tour Philadelphia in convincing fashion and has been a force of savagery ever since.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/D1R8%20Murray.JPG)

*Ben Murray is in the feature match area with 0 byes* 
But don't count out Ben Murray. Anytime someone is in the feature match area with no byes, it's because they have the goods – either in skill or in cards, or a little of both. When Estratti heard that Ben Murray had no byes he made a show of it.


"No byes?! Your deck must be good." He said. His eyes widened as he looked at his opponent in partial-facetious astonishment.


Murray nodded and the two shuffled up for the match.


### Game 1


Murray won the coin toss and elected to play. His first spell was a [Plummet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plummet) on Estratti's turn-two [Aven Squire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Squire). The American followed his kill spell with a [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser) and a [Canyon Minotaur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Canyon+Minotaur). Estratti made a [Crusader of Odric](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crusader+of+Odric), a [Mwonvuli Beast Tracker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mwonvuli+Beast+Tracker), then searched and played a [Sentinel Spider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sentinel+Spider).


During this time, Murray attacked the Italian down to 11 (Murray was still at 20) and played a [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist). Once the 4/4 spider came down from Estratti, Murray had to stop and think before he attempted to reduce his opponent's life total further. He rested his chin on his hands and passed the turn back after casting a second Arsonist and declining to attack. Not to be outdone by double creatures, the Pro Tour champion cast a second [Sentinel Spider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sentinel+Spider).


"You know you're only allowed to have one of those, right?" Murray said stone-faced.


Murray had a [Cleaver Riot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cleaver+Riot) in his hands and he was clearly trying to find an opening just wide enough to deal the remaining 11 damage. But Estratti was playing carefully, with his trademarked pained face, and made his moves with caution. After Murray made a [Flinthoof Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flinthoof+Boar) (fully charged), Estratti felt safe to attack with both vigilant spiders and his 4/4 [Crusade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crusade)r. Murray took 8 (12-11 in Murray's favor), and chump-blocked a creature with an Arsonist, taking out the [Tracker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tracker) on the gobbo's way out. [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) had taken out Murray's [Canyon Minotaur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Canyon+Minotaur) so now the Spiders were giving Estratti a clear, strong advantage.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/D1R8%20-%20Estratti.jpg)

*Samuele Estratti takes game one* 
Murray, after drawing yet-another land tapped down to one and made a desperation [Cleaver Riot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cleaver+Riot). He was hoping to trade his Boar and Courser for both of the Spiders, but a [Titanic Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Titanic+Growth) from Estratti saved one of the big guys. Left with only a [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist) on the board and land in his hand, Murray could only watch while Estratti just ran dudes into Murray's face until it exploded.


Samuele Estratti 1 – 0 Ben Murray


### Game 2


The two players started the second game with duel between a [Timberpack Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timberpack+Wolf) and its double. [Flinthoof Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flinthoof+Boar) broke the short-lived stalemate and gave Murray an early lead. A Yeva's Forcemage and another wolf attack from Estratti kept Murray's aggression some-what in check, but Murray had no fear about running his [Flinthoof Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flinthoof+Boar) right into a [Spiked Baloth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spiked+Baloth) the following turn. His eagerness for the trade was likely because Murray also had a [Bladetusk Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bladetusk+Boar) (which was quite unblockable) and a [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) incoming onto the battlefield. The score was 19-9 for Murray and the beast attack was still coming hard.




![Flinthoof Boar++Bladetusk Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Flinthoof%20Boar&options=)

![Flinthoof Boar++Bladetusk Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Bladetusk%20Boar&options=)
Estratti made a 3/3 [Primordial Hydra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primordial+Hydra), and declined to trade with the [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) the next turn. He choose instead to chump with the [Timberpack Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timberpack+Wolf) and sink to 6 life. Murray cast a post-combat Krenko's Command and passed the turn, watching the Hydra double its size to 6/6. In another turn it would be a trampling monstrosity.


Estratti shuffled his hand around and moved his fingers back and forth, counting invisible damage, wincing and remaking his face over and over. He attacked with the 6/6 and Murray tried to read his opponent while throwing a 1/1 goblin in front of it. A post-combat [Bloodhunter Bat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodhunter+Bat), made the scores closer – 19-8. However, after the next attack, Estratti sunk to 4 and a Chandra's Fury finished the job for Ben Murray.


Samuele Estratti 1 – 1 Ben Murray


### Game 3


Ben Murray kept an exciting hand this game. He knew Estratti was already going to Paris at least once and was on the play. So Murray kept a hand consisting [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite), [Cleaver Riot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cleaver+Riot) and land. I suppose his plan is to lay the land, then play [Thundermaw Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thundermaw+Hellkite), then give it double-strike. I mean, that's the way it appeared anyway.



![Cleaver Riot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Cleaver+Riot)

Estratti kept his six-card hand a cast the first creature with a 1/1 [Crusader of Odric](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crusader+of+Odric). A Yeva's Forcemage jumped alongside the [Crusade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crusade)r to take Murray to 16. Though Murray had some drawn spells of his own aside from his Plan A of giving a big dragon double-strike. He made a turn-three [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser) and turn-four [Primal Huntbeast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primal+Huntbeast). He was getting to the big guy. It was coming. The Timmy in him was bubbling below the surface, ready to explode.


But in the meantime, Estratti was turning up the heat on his side. On his next turn he cast both a Guardian of Akrasa and [Aven Squire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Squire) and attacked with a 6/6 [Crusade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crusade)r, sinking Murray to 10. It was 10-17 in Estratti's favor. But then Timmy came out to play. When the Hellkite came down, Estratti, who had been perched at the edge of his chair slumped backwards, hard. The attacks from all the creatures brought the Italian to 9. Was Plan A going to work?


Yup.


Though Estratti had another [Guardians of Akrasa](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Guardians+of+Akrasa) and attacked Murray to 4, everything was going according to Murray's inner Timmy. He untapped, cast [Cleaver Riot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cleaver+Riot), giving everything double-strike, and the giant, twice-hitting dragon of my ten-year-old **Magic** dreams flew over all Estratti's creatures and snatched away the Pro Tour champion's remaining life.


Ben Murray 2 – 1 Samuele Estratti


Like I said, don't discount anyone with zero byes. They've got the goods.




---


Saturday, 9:22 p.m. - Sealed Deck Exercise - pt. 3 With a (Sorin's) Vengeance\*
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*
\* - Please note, there is not actually a [Sorin's Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sorin%27s+Vengeance) in this Sealed deck exercise. The card is illegal in the *M13* Sealed format. If you register a [Sorin's Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sorin%27s+Vengeance) in your deck, it will not go well for you.


So we've reached the last installment of the Sealed deck exercise. The original plan was to only do two, but after Player's Championship combatant Luis Scott-Vargas took a swing at the deck, I really wanted to showcase the different ways to go with the pool. Scott-Vargas's build went back and forth in-between colors and strategies; there were some crazy little gambits considered and even taken. This session I did with Scott-Vargas was the first time I've ever heard a crowd go "Ooooo!" just while watching somebody build a deck. [Warning](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warning): Don't try this stuff at home, kids. LSV is a professional.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Sealed%20Ex%20Pt%203%20-%20LSV.jpg)

*LSV* 
The build started simple enough as Scott-Vargas sat down and immediately said, "Well, white is obvious. [Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sublime+Archangel) is simply the best and the rest is fine enough to carry it." As he shuffled through the white again he reiterated, "Yeah, it's fine." Though this feeling was universal among the other pros, he made slight card-evaluation deviations from those before him. For example, unlike Jon Finkel, LSV didn't immediately throw out [Mwonvuli Beast Tracker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mwonvuli+Beast+Tracker) when assessing the green part of the pool. But for the most part, all the players were on the same page at first blush.


On Blue, LSV quipped, "It's is just not as good as Black. [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) is so good with exalted." He continued, "And [Disentomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disentomb) and [Rise from the Grave](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rise+from+the+Grave) are so good when you are playing things like [Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sublime+Archangel) and Nighthawk."




![Vampire Nighthawk++Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Vampire%20Nighthawk&options=)

![Vampire Nighthawk++Sublime Archangel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Sublime%20Archangel&options=)
Scott-Vargas blazed through the Red and Green and built the White-Black deck that Finkel had built. He deviated from Finkel's build only by considering the [Veilborn Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Veilborn+Ghoul) and the two aforementioned Raise-Dead-like cards.


By this point a crowd was beginning to gather. Both pros and amateurs were watching LSV shift cards around and back and forth. Ben Stark yelled from the peanut gallery to cut [Disentomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disentomb). "You're not going to play that and you know it." Scott-Vargas cut the card, but kept it close. He was at 23 spells when he went through the leftover cards one last time. The deck looked very similar to Finkel's and everyone was talking to the person next to them about what slight changes they would make, while agreeing the deck looked good.


But then Luis paused on the [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds). He quickly cut the three worst cards and added two [Krenko's Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krenko%27s+Command) and [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer). This was when the crowd made that audible "Oooooo" sound.


Josh Utter-Leyton said, "I have to take another look at your Sealed pool for the GP." He was referring to the fact that Scott-Vargas was playing quite an ugly four-color beast in the main event, and was wondering if it actually had to be so ugly or if Scott-Vargas was just being really greedy.


The onlookers had not been aware of the three fetch lands sitting under Luis's other cards, and when he broke them out, everyone understood. The pros immediately started looking at the rest of the Player's Championship-qualified pool to see what could be splashed.


During this rummaging, Luis turned to me and told me his problem with the current build is that he'd only ever have one [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) on the field at a time, and [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer) is at its best with more than that. Ben Stark, who was rifling through the stack said, "Why don't you go White-Red?" In a flash the Black was out and the Red was in. The new build resembled what Tom Martell was talking about except the [Planar Cleansing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Planar+Cleansing) was still in, as was a [Fervor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fervor). All the pros seemed to take notice of how good the deck was looking. The skeptics were starting to warm up.


Scott-Vargas, after surveying the new look, summarized, "White-Black is pretty good, but this gives you a much better curve. Your two-drops are better and you're not dependent on the top end." This echoed Sam Black's statements earlier. So the deck, though slightly different, now resembled Tom Martell's plan.


And then Scott-Vargas made the crowd groan again.


He took out the mediocre cards and tossed in [Essence Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Essence+Drain), [Bloodhunter Bat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodhunter+Bat), [Crimson Muckwader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crimson+Muckwader) and a [Switcheroo](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Switcheroo). Someone in the audience did a face-palm and both Utter-Leyton, Stark and now David Ochoa condemned this gluttonous, but all-too-common Luis-like decision. They told him to at least cut the [Switcheroo](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Switcheroo) for [Mark of the Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mark+of+the+Vampire). And the card went in and out during a couple iterations of the build.




![Essence Drain++Crimson Muckwader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Essence%20Drain&options=)

![Essence Drain++Crimson Muckwader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Crimson%20Muckwader&options=)
Though we likely could have continued these mutations ad infinitum, as everyone seemed to be having fun, the next round was getting ready to start. At the end of this delightful session, Luis had a White-Red-splash-Black-and-possibly-Blue build. After going back and forth he scooped the cards into a pile, handed them to me and said, "Here's the deck. I got it."


Here's what it looked like:







#### Luis Scott-Vargas


#####

##### Preto (2)



1

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Evolving+Wilds)


















It was a wonderful looking pile. In my mind, he had taken a simple Sealed pool and made art. It was a living embodiment of a [Switcheroo](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Switcheroo).


I can't even begin to make the land work for this deck. LSV was off and running to check his pairings and left me to wonder how to add land to this masterpiece. What is up in the list right now is just my place-holder, please don't take it seriously. Though, there was one lingering question I still had for the land. I doubt even LSV would do such a thing, but the pile he handed me did include the [Hellion Crucible](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hellion+Crucible). But surely no one's that crazy. Right?


A bunch of different Pros, a bunch of different decks. Which pro's deck did your build most resemble?




---


Round 9 Feature Match - Martin Juza vs. Whit Froehlich
------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
Whit Froehlich – no relation to Eric Froehlich, no matter what his Twitter account will have you believe – is a Michigan native and Amherst student who has been tearing through the field all day with, quite simply, one of the best decks in the room.


Just listen...


"Did you have three byes?" Martin Juza asked Froehlich as they sat down.


"No byes."


"So your deck's very good," Juza said, frowning a bit.


"I've won some games."


Cold, man, cold.


"Some" games was at least 14 at this point, as both players had racked up seven match wins with just a single loss each, only Juza had three byes to get him to this point.


It's also worth noting that Juza is one of the fortunate 16 players playing in the Players Championship this upcoming week. We'll do a roundup next round of how all of the 15 competitors in attendance this weekend have done today, giving a slight preview of the upcoming All-Star contest.


### Game 1


Froehlich chose to draw first, the first time I had seen any player make such a choice all weekend.


It's a bold strategy, Cotton. Let's see if it pays off.


Juza started with a pair of one drops in [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton) and [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist), accidentally flashing the [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer) in his hand that would make that Arsonist something to be truly feared.



![Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Goblin+Arsonist)

Froehlich, riding high on his extra card, curved an [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) into [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk), surely a future target for that [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer) in Juza's hand.


[Yeva, Nature's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yeva%2C+Nature%27s+Herald) jumped into play for Juza at the end of Froehlich's fourth turn, only to be met with Froehlich's own copy of the flashy Green Legend. After losing his beater, Juza simply killed [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) with a [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear) and left mana up to pump his [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton).


Froehlich, however, offed the offending artifact beater with [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) – an uncommon interaction that has been all too common this weekend – then cast a second copy of the five-mana 2/2 to destroy one of Juza's [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain)s the following turn. Juza had managed to play a [Furnace Whelp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Furnace+Whelp), but was losing the race.


"Your deck is pretty sweet," the Czech superstar offered as Froehlich continued to back him into a corner with a [Timberpack Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timberpack+Wolf).


[Farseek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Farseek) helped Juza get back up to four lands, but he was clearly trying to get to five to take immediate advantage of his [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer). He got there, but Froehlich [Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder)ed the [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist) in response to keep Juza from abusing the uncommon Goblin.


On the next attack, Juza traded his [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer) and [Furnace Whelp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Furnace+Whelp) for both [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime)s, clearing his side of the battlefield, but also leaving Froehlich with just a [Timberpack Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timberpack+Wolf) for offense.


At this point, Froehlich had 16 life to Juza's 10.



![Mwonvuli Beast Tracker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mwonvuli+Beast+Tracker)

Juza, now getting back on his feet, played [Mwonvuli Beast Tracker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mwonvuli+Beast+Tracker) to fetch up a [Primal Huntbeast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primal+Huntbeast). Froehlich played a second wolf on his turn, and the 3/3s traded on the American's next attack.


By now it had become apparent that Froehlich was extremely flooded, and when his second [Timberpack Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timberpack+Wolf) traded with an [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) and a [Chandra's Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chandra%27s+Fury), he was suddenly without any action at all.


An [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary) of his own gave Froehlich a [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser), but Juza simply killed it with [Turn to Slag](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Turn+to+Slag).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Round%209%20Juza.JPG)

*For every move Martin Juza made, Whit Froehlich seemed to have an answer.* 
With the life totals knotted at 6 each, Juza resolved a [Spiked Baloth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spiked+Baloth) to face down a [Walking Corpse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Walking+Corpse), but Froehlich one-upped him with [Xathrid Gorgon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Xathrid+Gorgon). Juza passed once again, and it appeared he might be just as flooeded as Froehlich was.


[Mutilate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutilate) from Froehlich drew a look of surprise from Juza, but that and a [Sentinel Spider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sentinel+Spider) were enough to convince him to concede when he drew yet another land off the top.


Froehlich 1 – Juza 0


### Game 2


Juza sideboarded more than a few cards for the second game of the series, and even put Froehlich on the draw again, likely right where they both wanted to be.


Even playing second, Froehlich started first with an [Elvish Visionary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Visionary), but had kept a hand with no black sources plus [Mutilate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutilate) and [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk).


Juza made his first play with a [Mwonvuli Beast Tracker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mwonvuli+Beast+Tracker) searching for...


"Nothing," Juza said, giving his deck a gamely shuffle anyway.


Froehlich, finding his first [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp), went slightly bigger with a [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser), but held it back on defense to face down [Spiked Baloth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spiked+Baloth). Juza didn't bite and instead cast a [Furnace Whelp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Furnace+Whelp) without attacking.




![Essence Drain++Crimson Muckwader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Essence%20Drain&options=)

![Essence Drain++Crimson Muckwader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Crimson%20Muckwader&options=)
That, of course, just gave Froehlich the perfect opportunity to draw a second [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp) and sweep the board with [Mutilate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mutilate), save for his 3/3 [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser).


Juza gave a little smile, nodded his head and cast [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton) and [Primal Huntbeast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primal+Huntbeast).


When Froehlich attacked the next turn, Juza asked him how many cards he had in hand.


"Six."


"I feel like I'm playing the wrong format here," Juza said, holding just two cards and increasingly falling behind despite an otherwise solid draw.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/Round%209%20Froehlich.JPG)

*"Hm, so if I 2-for-1 him here, 2-for-1 him next round, then I can get a 3-for-1 the round after that," though Whit Froehlich every turn of the tournament.* 
Two Elvish Visionaries kept the cards flowing for Juza, but his force was once again outclassed as Froehlich flashed in [Yeva, Nature's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yeva%2C+Nature%27s+Herald). Juza then simply shrugged as his [Primal Huntbeast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Primal+Huntbeast) traded for Froehlich's [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser). Froehlich, in turn, shrugged as he played [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk).


But when he attempted to use [Prey Upon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prey+Upon) with the Nighthawk to kill [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton), Juza was ready with the [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear). Considering Froehlich had a 4/4 Yeva on the battlefield, the play was perhaps a bit greedy.


Not that it seemed to matter, as his cards simply outclassed Juza's at every turn, including when an [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) killed [Chronomaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chronomaton) ... again.


[Chandra's Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chandra%27s+Fury) let Juza's Elvish Visionaries trade for Froehlich's 2/2s, but [Rise from the Grave](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rise+from+the+Grave) brought back [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk), and it appeared the writing was on the wall. Not even an [Arms Dealer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arms+Dealer) could stop the inevitable.


"I think your deck is a little better than mine," Juza said, scooping up his cards, left with the consolation that, at 7-2, he was still a lock for Day 2.


Froehlich 2 – Juza 0




---


Saturday, 10:44 p.m. - Tracking the Players Championship Participants
---------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
Besides just being an awesomely large tournament, Grand Prix Boston-Worcester is also a preview of sorts for the Players Championship happening this upcoming week.


With 15 of the participants for the first-ever 16-man tournament playing here this weekend (World Champion Jun'ya Iyanaga is the lone exception), we get a pretty good view of those player's chops in ***Magic** 2013* limited, one of the formats that will be featured when the action shifts to Seattle on Wednesday.


So let's take a peek and see how the famous 15 did after 9 rounds (the cut for Day 2 was after 9 rounds, though a 10th round of sealed is being played today). Six of the 15 players were among the 240 who made the cut to Day 2.


2011 Player of the Year Owen Turtenwald: 4-3 (dropped after Round 7)


2011 **Magic Online** Champion Reid Duke: 7-2 (won Round 9 to make the cut)


Pro Tour Philadelphia Winner Samuele Estratti: 6-3 (lost Round 9 to miss the cut)


Pro Tour *Dark Ascension* Winner Brian Kibler: 5-3 (dropped after Round 8)


Pro Tour *Avacyn Restored* Winner Alexander Hayne: 5-4


Top Pro Points in North America, Josh Utter-Leyton: 3-3 (dropped after Round 6)


Top Pro Points in Latin America, Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa: 8-1


Top Pro Points in Europe, Martin Juza: 7-2


Top Pro Points in Japan, Yuuya Watanabe: 6-3 (lost Round 9 to miss the cut)


Top Pro Points in the Asian Pacific, Tzu Ching Kuo: 3-3 (dropped after Round 6)


At-large invitees (top Pro Points not already invited)


Jon Finkel: 8-1


Luis Scott-Vargas: 6-3 (lost his win-and-in round)


Shouta Yasooka: 8-1


David Ochoa: 5-4


Shuhei Nakamura: 8-1


And here it is in the order of how they finished:


Shuhei Nakamura: 8-1


Shouta Yasooka: 8-1


Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa: 8-1


Jon Finkel: 8-1


Martin Juza: 7-2


Reid Duke: 7-2


Samuele Estratti: 6-3


Luis Scott-Vargas: 6-3


Yuuya Watanabe: 6-3


Brian Kibler: 5-3


Alexander Hayne: 5-4


David Ochoa: 5-4


Owen Turtenwald: 4-3


Tzu Ching Kuo: 3-3


Josh Utter-Leyton: 3-3


Is this a taste of things to come or can the players who didn't make the cut flip the script? Tune in later this week to find out. In the meantime, find more information on the Players Championship and the 16 players vying for the title at <http://www.wizards.com/magic/tcg/events.aspx?x=mtg/event/playerschamp/2012/main>.




---


Saturday, 11:19 p.m. - Quick Hits: If you could have four copies of any common card in your Sealed pool, what would it be?
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/QH1%20-%20Scott-Vargas%20%28with%20Martell%29.jpg)*Luis Scott-Vargas - "Probably [Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder). The card is just so good. I don’t know why I wouldn’t want more of them."* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/QH1%20-%20Sharfman.jpg)*David Sharfman – " I think my answer on any other day would be [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear), but look at my outfit! I'm saying [Kraken Hatchling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kraken+Hatchling). Wait, wait, [Horseshoe Crab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Horseshoe+Crab). That's much more lobster-like. [I was wondering why he didn't say [Rock Lobster](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rock+Lobster) myself.]"* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/QH1%20-%20Tom%20Martell.JPG)*Tom Martell - "I'm going to answer as if you'd said four copies of any two cards, because then the answer would Krenko's Command and [Trumpet Blast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trumpet+Blast). I like that better than your question."* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/QH%20-%20Juza.jpg)*Martin Juza – "If Blue weren't terrible, definitely [Divination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divination). But you don't draw into anything good with it – just more Blue cards. So, my first thought is [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear), but there are definitely some other good ones. Four [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds) would allow me to play every bomb I got, and four [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies) would be pretty nuts."* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/QH1%20-%20Conley%20Woods.JPG)*Conley Woods – "I like [Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder), but it's definitely not [Murder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murder). The card's not splashable enough. I think the answer is [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear), because it stacks so well. It can kill creatures or go to the face. Although, I think [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism) is a good answer too. Either [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism) or [Searing Spear](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Searing+Spear)."* 




---


Round 10 Feature Match - Rob Dougherty vs. Craig Wescoe
-------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro*
Craig Wescoe pulled out a happy-face dice and said, "Whoever rolls the happiest face wins. Ok?" He then explained the different faces of the dice and rolled a "kinda-sad" face. He was disappointed, but Rob Dougherty was more so when he rolled the "awfully sad" face. Oddly enough, the faces aptly represented their expressions after the roll. Wescoe had won the face-roll.


Though both these players had already made it into Day Two, as the cut-off was last round, there was one more round of **Magic** to be played before they could rest up for the drafting tomorrow.


"I'll let you go first, because you look really sad," Wescoe said. Dougherty graciously accepted.


### Game 1


Rob Dougherty went first and opened a [Dragon Hatchling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragon+Hatchling). The baby attacked for zero the next turn and then Dougherty laid a [Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser). He put his hand on the baby dragon and said, "He just wanted to get in there," as he passed the turn to Wescoe.



![Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Harbor+Bandit)

Craig Wescoe answered with a [Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit) (fully 3/3) and traded it with the Courser the next turn. Dougherty refueled with a [Canyon Minotaur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Canyon+Minotaur), also known as "[Centaur Courser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Courser) for One More Mana" and passed the turn back. Wescoe laid a Vampire Nighthawk, and goaded, "Let the dragon attack now." The next turn he laid a [Scroll Thief](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scroll+Thief) and made the totals 18-19 in his favor.


[Canyon Minotaur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Canyon+Minotaur) and an [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) (which had taken out an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)) crashed towards Wescoe and sunk him to 14. A [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) from Dougherty soon followed. "Is that all you got?" Wescoe asked, then laid down a [Giant Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Scorpion). The Nighthawk made the totals 21-16.


Dougherty had an even bigger beast than the [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) waiting in his hands. He had the mother of all big dudes, the [Hamletback Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hamletback+Goliath). He still needed one mana to cast it, but he knew getting the Scorpion out of the way before playing the giant would be integral. So Dougherty attacked with the Slime, the Hatchling and the 'Tusk. The Scorpion took out Tusker-doo, getting the Hall-of-Famer a 3/3 beast in the process; and the totals adjusted to 21-12.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/D1R10%20Wescoe.jpg)

*Craig Wescoe* 
Wescoe passed with all his mana untapped. He had mentioned before that the reason his deck has had success was not because it had powerful cards, but because it has the ability to stop powerful cards. Dougherty was throwing a lot of powerful cards in his general direction and we would have to see if Wescoe's deck really had the stopping power he referred to.


Slime, Minotaur, [Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Beast) and a new [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies) went into the attack zone. A flashed [Faerie Invaders](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faerie+Invaders) traded with the [Canyon Minotaur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Canyon+Minotaur). The rest of the business got through and Wescoe went to 4. Dougherty had two cards left in his hand. One of which was the Goliath. He flashed the other one to Wescoe, which caused him to scoop up his cards. It was a Chandra's Fury.


Rob Dougherty 1 – 0 Craig Wescoe


As Wescoe shuffled for the next game he said to his opponent, "I was wondering if you had any non-creature spells in there – that Chandra's Fury."


"Yeah. It's all fatties and Fury." Dougherty replied.


"As far as I can tell." Wescoe finished shuffling and presented his deck. He again chose to draw.


### Game 2


Dougherty mulliganed once, then led with an [Evolving Wilds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Evolving+Wilds) into a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain). He played a [Deadly Recluse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadly+Recluse), which ended up as a perfect counter to the [Welkin Tern](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Welkin+Tern) Wescoe played right after. Dougherty used his spider to attack, then cast a [Dragon Hatchling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragon+Hatchling). Like last game, Wescoe laid a [Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit) and passed the turn back.


Dougherty was on the beat-down plan until he drew a [Sands of Delirium](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sands+of+Delirium). He thought for a bit and laid it down. Now it was Wescoe who would be on the aggression. Wescoe cast a [Duskmantle Prowler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskmantle+Prowler) and sent in a 3/2 [Welkin Tern](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Welkin+Tern). Dougherty declined to block and milled Wescoe for one before he untapped. The milled card was a [Hamletback Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hamletback+Goliath).



![Duskmantle Prowler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Duskmantle+Prowler)

"You're not the only one with Giants in your deck!" Wescoe smiled. "Although now you might be." The he frowned.


Dougherty gave Wescoe another cause for sadness when he cast a [Flames of the Firebrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flames+of+the+Firebrand) which killed both the Tern and the Prowler. Wescoe, undeterred, followed with another exalter in [Servant of Nefarox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Servant+of+Nefarox) and took Dougherty to 11 with an unblockable [Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit). It was 11-19 when the Hall-of-Famer milled two more cards off of Wescoe's library. However, for this mill plan to work, Dougherty was going to have to find an answer to a 4/4 unblockable dude. And right quick. Dougherty went to 7, then 3. This is not working Dougherty; I mean, quicker.


On his last turn, Dougherty drew [Titanic Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Titanic+Growth). If he were going the damage route, this would've been helpful, but now, all he did was mill some more cards before he was killed so he had just a bit more information for the next game.


Dougherty looked. [Void Stalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Void+Stalker), [Talrand, Sky Summoner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Talrand%2C+Sky+Summoner) (foil, too) [Public Execution](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Public+Execution) and [Negate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Negate) were the pertinent cards. And after getting a good look-see, Dougherty scooped for the final battle.


Rob Dougherty 1 – 1 Craig Wescoe


### Game 3


Wescoe went first and on turn two he posited, "Are you ready for the beating?! BAM!" Wescoe slammed down a 0/4 [Kraken Hatchling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kraken+Hatchling).


Dougherty again had to choose between the aggressive plan of [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies), [Bladetusk Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bladetusk+Boar)s, [Dragon Hatchling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragon+Hatchling)s and the like, and the [Sands of Delirium](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sands+of+Delirium) he had again in his hand. He laid a [Dragon Hatchling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragon+Hatchling) to join his [Deadly Recluse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadly+Recluse) and passed the turn.


"So there's three creatures on the board and a total power of one?" Wescoe was a little amused by both the player's decks revolving around slowing the board to a stall and then winning big. Next turn, Wescoe offered a trade of his new [Vampire Nighthawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Nighthawk) with Dougherty's [Deadly Recluse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadly+Recluse) and Dougherty accepted. The [Sands of Delirium](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sands+of+Delirium) came down, then a [Bladetusk Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bladetusk+Boar) from Dougherty the following turn. The scores were 20-21.




![Deadly Recluse++Sands of Delirium](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Deadly%20Recluse&options=)

![Deadly Recluse++Sands of Delirium](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Sands%20of%20Delirium&options=)
[Duskmantle Prowler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskmantle+Prowler) changed that life total in a jiffy for Wescoe and he again had some pressure on the board. But the Boar was equal pressure from Dougherty and the [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) the next turn? Well I guess that was more pressure. Combined with the [Millstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Millstone) for X (that sounds a bit like a Prog Rock band name), Dougherty was seemingly ahead in all counts. It was 22-18 and Wescoe had 24 cards left in his library.


But don't count Craig Wescoe out, he's kind of made a career out of powering through and succeeding when people don't expect him to. He took the beastly damage, then made a [Faerie Invaders](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faerie+Invaders). After it attacked on Wescoe's next turn, the totals was 18-15 (Wescoe went down to 17 cards in his library). Wescoe added a [Harbor Bandit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Harbor+Bandit) and a [Giant Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Scorpion) to complicate matters further. When Dougherty got his turn back, he had to think about where things should go. He had a [Prey Upon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prey+Upon), but anything he wanted to kill would also kill his [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk), and every mana he spent was one fewer card milled.


Dougherty eventually sent in the beasts. The [Giant Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Scorpion) stung the [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk) and left behind a slightly smaller [Thragtusk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thragtusk). Dougherty made a [Canyon Minotaur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Canyon+Minotaur) and a [Mogg Flunkies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mogg+Flunkies) before passing the turn back. It was 18-12, with 16 cards in the library. But Wescoe made another two exalted creatures and attacked the totals to 12-12.




![Deadly Recluse++Sands of Delirium](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Deadly%20Recluse&options=)

![Deadly Recluse++Sands of Delirium](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?size=small&type=card&name=Sands%20of%20Delirium&options=)
After Dougherty made the Faerie [Plummet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plummet), all his creatures came in. The [Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Beast), the Boar, the Flunkies, the Minotaur and the Hatchling. [Duskmantle Prowler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskmantle+Prowler) blocked the 3/3 [Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Beast), [Servant of Nefarox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Servant+of+Nefarox) took out the [Canyon Minotaur](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Canyon+Minotaur) and the rest went through. Dougherty pumped the Dragon for three and the totals became 12-3.


When Wescoe drew his card for the turn, he gave an involuntary shrug and rolled his eyes a bit. I don't think it was a very good draw to get when you're at 3 and staring down at least nine point of damage the next turn. Wescoe attacked for four damage with the Bandit, then sacrificed it to a [Disciple of Bolas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disciple+of+Bolas). He gained four life (8-7) and drew four cards (10 cards left in the library). Wescoe laid a [Watercourser](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Watercourser) and passed the turn back. Two more cards in his library hit the bin. There were eight cards left for Wescoe and Dougherty had eight untapped lands.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbos12/D1R10%20Dougherty.JPG)

*Congratulations for Rob Dougherty in his win over Wescoe* 
Dougherty did the final points with flying [Dragon Hatchling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragon+Hatchling) and an unblockable [Bladetusk Boar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bladetusk+Boar) instead.


Rob Dougherty 2 – 1 Craig Wescoe


What made Dougherty's deck perform so well was the dual attack paths that [Sands of Delirium](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sands+of+Delirium) allowed. If Wescoe committed resources to stop the milling, he would have lost to damage and vice versa. The appearance of the artifact made Wescoe try to split his resources and it just didn't work. That card is dangerous.




---
